NewServiceAccount returns an admission.Interface implementation which limits admission of Pod CREATE requests based on the pod's ServiceAccount:\n95: // 1. If the pod does not specify a ServiceAccount, it sets the pod's ServiceAccount to \"default\"\n96: // 2. It ensures the ServiceAccount referenced by the pod exists\n97: // 3. The key decision function is `shouldAutomount()` (line 254), which implements a precedence hierarchy: pod-level `AutomountServiceAccountToken` setting overrides service account-level setting, which defaults to true for backwards compatibility. When enabled, the `mountServiceAccountToken()` method (line 416) injects volume projections into the pod spec using `TokenVolumeSource()` (line 485), which creates a projected volume containing the service account token with path 'token' and an expiration seconds value. The `Admit()` method (line 138) is the main entry point that runs during pod creation, checks if `MountServiceAccountToken` is enabled, and conditionally calls the mounting logic. The `TokensController` type (line 133) manages the lifecycle of ServiceAccountToken secrets - it watches both ServiceAccount and Secret objects, creating token secrets when service accounts are created and cleaning them up when accounts are deleted.
